Whereas photons emitted from the solar core may require 40,000 years to diffuse to the outer layers of the Sun, neutrinos generated in stellar fusion reactions at the core cross this distance practically unimpeded at nearly the speed of light.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[108]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Neutrinos are also useful for probing astrophysical sources beyond the Solar System because they are the only known particles that are not significantly <a href="/wiki/Attenuation" title="Attenuation">attenuated</a> by their travel through the interstellar medium. Optical photons can be obscured or diffused by dust, gas, and background radiation. High-energy <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cosmic_rays" title="Cosmic rays">cosmic rays</a>, in the form of swift protons and atomic nuclei, are unable to travel more than about 100 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megaparsec" title="Megaparsec">megaparsecs</a> due to the <a href="/wiki/Greisen%E2%80%93Zatsepin%E2%80%93Kuzmin_limit" title="Greisen&#8211;Zatsepin&#8211;Kuzmin limit">Greisen&#8211;Zatsepin&#8211;Kuzmin limit</a> (GZK cutoff). Neutrinos, in contrast, can travel even greater distances barely attenuated.\n</p><p>The galactic core of the <a href="/wiki/Milky_Way" title="Milky Way">Milky Way</a> is fully obscured by dense gas and numerous bright objects. Neutrinos produced in the galactic core might be measurable by Earth-based <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neutrino_telescope" title="Neutrino telescope">neutrino telescopes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Close2012_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-Close2012-19">[17]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Another important use of the neutrino is in the observation of <a href="/wiki/Supernova" title="Supernova">supernovae</a>, the explosions that end the lives of highly massive stars. The core collapse phase of a supernova is an extremely dense and energetic event. It is so dense that no known particles are able to escape the advancing core front except for neutrinos. Consequently, supernovae are known to release approximately 99% of their radiant energy in a short (10-second) burst of neutrinos.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[109]</a></sup> These neutrinos are a very useful probe for core collapse studies.\n</p><p>The rest mass of the neutrino is an important test of cosmological and astrophysical theories (see <i><a href="/wiki/Dark_matter" title="Dark matter">Dark matter</a></i>). The neutrino\'s significance in probing cosmological phenomena is as great as any other method, and is thus a major focus of study in astrophysical communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SciAm-Gelmini_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-SciAm-Gelmini-114">[110]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The study of neutrinos is important in <a href="/wiki/Particle_physics" title="Particle physics">particle physics</a> because neutrinos typically have the lowest mass, and hence are examples of the lowest-energy particles theorized in extensions of the <a href="/wiki/Standard_Model" title="Standard Model">Standard Model</a> of particle physics.\n</p><p>In November 2012, American scientists used a particle accelerator to send a coherent neutrino message through 780 feet of rock. This marks the first use of neutrinos for communication, and future research may permit binary neutrino messages to be sent immense distances through even the densest materials, such as the Earth\'s core.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[111]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July&#160;2018, the <a href="/wiki/IceCube_Neutrino_Observatory" title="IceCube Neutrino Observatory">IceCube Neutrino Observatory</a> announced that they have traced an extremely-high-energy neutrino that hit their Antarctica-based research station in September 2017 back to its point of origin in the <a href="/wiki/Blazar" title="Blazar">blazar</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TXS_0506_%2B056" title="TXS 0506 +056">TXS 0506 +056</a> located 3.7&#160;billion <a href="/wiki/Light-year" title="Light-year">light-years</a> away in the direction of the constellation <a href="/wiki/Orion_(constellation)" title="Orion (constellation)">Orion</a>. This is the first time that a <a href="/wiki/Neutrino_detector" title="Neutrino detector">neutrino detector</a> has been used to locate an object in space and that a source of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cosmic_rays" title="Cosmic rays">cosmic rays</a> has been identified.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20180712_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20180712-116">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[114]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neutrino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: See id="cite_note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">More specifically, Pauli postulated what is now called the <i>electron neutrino</i>. Two other types were discovered later: <i>see</i> <a href="#Neutrino_flavors_anchor">Neutrino flavor</a> <i>below</i>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Niels_Bohr" title="Niels Bohr">Niels Bohr</a> was notably opposed to this interpretation of beta decay &#8211; he was ready to accept that energy, momentum, and angular momentum were not conserved quantities at the atomic level.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-46"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-46">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In this context, "light neutrino" means neutrinos with less than half the mass of the Z&#160;boson.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-96"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-96">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Like all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thermal_power_plant" title="Thermal power plant">thermal power plants</a>, only about one third of the heat generated can be converted to electricity, so a <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7009400000000000000&#9824;</span>4000&#160;MW</span> reactor would produce only <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7009130000000000000&#9824;</span>1300&#160;MW</span> of electric power, with <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7009270000000000000&#9824;</span>2700&#160;MW</span> being <a href="/wiki/Waste_heat" title="Waste heat">waste heat</a>.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neutrino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-Mertens-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Mertens_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Mertens_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Mertens_1-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Mertens_1-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Mertens_1-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Mertens, Susanne (2016). "Direct neutrino mass experiments". <i>Journal of Physics: Conference Series</i>. <b>718</b> (2): 022013. <a href="/wiki/ArXiv" title="ArXiv">arXiv</a>:<span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="//arxiv.org/abs/1605.01579" rel="nofollow">1605.01579</a></span>. <a href="/wiki/Bibcode" title="Bibcode">Bibcode</a>:<a class="external text"
